style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="s05083565801DA9906720BFF72D44017C"></a><div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div></div><br><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-weight:bold;">Introductory Note</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">On January 14, 2015, the Board of Directors of Target Corporation (&#8220;Target&#8221;) determined to exit Target&#8217;s Canadian operations following a review of Target&#8217;s Canadian performance and a review of potential alternative operating scenarios.  In connection with the plan approved by the Board of Directors, on January 15, 2015, Target Canada Co. and certain other wholly owned subsidiaries of Target (the &#8220;Applicants&#8221;) filed for protection (the &#8220;Filing&#8221;) under the </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-style:italic;">Companies&#8217; Creditors Arrangement Act</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;(Canada) (&#8220;CCAA&#8221;) with the Ontario Superior Court of Justice (Commercial List) in Toronto (the &#8220;Court&#8221;).  The Applicants, along with certain limited partnerships to which the Applicants are seeking to extend protections in the CCAA process (collectively, &#8220;Target Canada&#8221;), comprise substantially all of Target&#8217;s Canadian operations and Target&#8217;s Canadian Segment.  Target Canada intends to engage in a fair and orderly liquidation process, subject to the Court&#8217;s approval, and expects that stores in Canada will remain open during the contemplated liquidation process.  </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">The Applicants will be deconsolidated from Target&#8217;s financial statements as of the Filing date.  To effect the deconsolidation, Target will account for its investment in Target Canada using the cost method of accounting.  Target&#8217;s historical Canadian Segment will be treated as discontinued operations in the fourth quarter ending January 31, 2015.  As a result, Target will now operate as a single U.S. segment.  </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-weight:bold;">Item 1.01.  </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-weight:bold;text-decoration:underline;">Entry into a Material Definitive Agreement</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-weight:bold;">.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">In connection with the Filing, Target has committed to provide to certain of the Target Canada entities a debtor-in-possession credit facility to permit Target Canada to finance operations during the CCAA process (the &#8220;DIP Facility&#8221;).  The terms of the DIP Facility are subject to approval by the Court and include the following:</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;padding-left:0px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">The maximum amount available under the DIP Facility will be US$175 million.</font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;padding-left:0px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Loans will bear interest at a rate of 5% per annum.  Upon an event of default, the rate will increase to 7% per annum until the maturity date.  </font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;padding-left:0px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">No fees will be charged to Target Canada.</font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;padding-left:0px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Loans under the DIP Facility will be secured by all of Target Canada&#8217;s property subject to certain exceptions.</font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;padding-left:0px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">The maturity date will be the earliest of: (i) the date on which the stay of proceedings in the CCAA process finally expires without being extended; (ii) the date on which the CCAA proceedings are terminated; or (iii) January 15, 2016, or such later date as may be agreed.  All outstanding obligations under the DIP Facility will be due and payable on the maturity date.</font></div></td></tr></table><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A copy of the term sheet comprising the DIP Facility will be filed as an Exhibit to Target&#8217;s Annual Report on Form 10-K for the year ending January 31, 2015.  </font></div><div Filing described in the Introductory Note, Target has determined that the Applicants will be deconsolidated from Target&#8217;s financial statements as of the date of the Filing.  </font></div><div Canada Co. to ensure payment of certain amounts; and</font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">The appointment of representative counsel to represent employees of Target Canada Co. in the CCAA proceedings.    </font></div></td></tr></table><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><br><div><div name="s05083565801DA9906720BFF72D44017C"></a><div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div></div><br><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-weight:bold;">Item 2.05.  </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-weight:bold;text-decoration:underline;">Costs Associated with Exit or Disposal Activities</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-weight:bold;">.  </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Target expects to accrue approximately $390 million pre-tax for exit losses in its discontinued operations in the fourth quarter ending January 31, 2015, all of which are expected to require cash expenditures.  These exit losses include probable losses relating to certain claims that may be asserted against Target as a result of Target&#8217;s guaranty of certain obligations of Target Canada Co. or other claims that may be made against Target, and Target&#8217;s expected cash contribution of approximately C$70 million (approximately US$59 million) into a trust for the benefit of the employees of Target Canada Co.  Given the early stage of the exit activities, Target&#8217;s estimates of probable losses are based on currently available information and assessment of the validity of certain claims.  These estimates may change as new information becomes available and it is reasonably possible that Target may incur a material loss in excess of the amount accrued.   </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-weight:bold;">Item 2.06.  </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-weight:bold;text-decoration:underline;">Material Impairment</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-weight:bold;">.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Target expects to impair its investment in Target Canada based on the estimated fair value of Target Canada&#8217;s net assets.  This impairment, along with the impairment of certain other related assets outside of Target Canada, is expected to result in a non-cash, pre-tax impairment charge of approximately $4.8 billion in Target&#8217;s discontinued operations in the fourth quarter ending January 31, 2015.   </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:174%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-weight:bold;">Item 7.01.  </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-weight:bold;text-decoration:underline;">Regulation FD Disclosure</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-weight:bold;">.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Target expects to report pre-tax losses from discontinued operations of approximately $5.4 billion in the fourth quarter ending January 31, 2015, which consist of:</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">January 15, 2015) &#8212; Today Target Corporation (NYSE:TGT) (the "Company") announces that it plans to discontinue operating stores in Canada through its indirect wholly-owned subsidiary, Target Canada Co. (&#8220;Target Canada&#8221;). As a part of that process, this morning Target Canada filed an application for protection under the Companies&#8217; Creditors Arrangement Act (the &#8220;CCAA&#8221;) with the Ontario Superior Court of Justice (Commercial List) in Toronto (the &#8220;Court&#8221;).</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8220;When I joined Target, I promised our team and shareholders that I would take a hard look at our business and operations in an effort to improve our performance and transform our company. After a thorough review of our Canadian performance and careful consideration of the implications of all options, we were unable to find a realistic scenario that would get Target Canada to profitability until at least 2021. Personally, this was a very difficult decision, but it was the right decision for our company. With the full support of Target Corporation's Board of Directors, we have determined that it is in the best interest of our business and our shareholders to exit the Canadian market and focus on driving growth and building further momentum in our U.S. business,&#8221; said Brian Cornell, Target Corporation Chairman and CEO. </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:center;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8211; more &#8211;</font></div><br><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="sADE64D2CA3AB34478F71BFF72DF2D4EA"></a><div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div></div><br><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-style:italic;">Target Corporation Announces Plans to Discontinue Canadian Operations &#8211; Page 2 of 5</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Target Canada currently has 133 stores across the country and employs approximately 17,600 people. To ensure fair treatment of Target Canada employees, Target Corporation is seeking the Court&#8217;s approval to voluntarily make cash contributions of C$70 million (approximately US$59 million) into an Employee Trust. Upon approval by the Court, the proposed trust would provide that nearly all Target Canada-based employees receive a minimum of 16 weeks of compensation, including wages and benefits coverage for employees who are not required for the full wind-down period. Target Canada stores will remain open during the liquidation process.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">As part of its application, Target Canada is seeking the appointment of Alvarez &amp; Marsal Canada as Monitor in the CCAA proceedings to oversee the liquidation and wind-down process for Target Canada and its subsidiaries. Subject to Court approval, Target Corporation has committed to provide a US$175 million debtor-in-possession credit facility to finance Target Canada&#8217;s operations during the CCAA proceedings. Target Canada is also seeking Court approval to engage Lazard to advise Target Canada in connection with the sale of its real estate assets. </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8220;The Target Canada team has worked tirelessly to improve the fundamentals, fix operations and build a deeper relationship with our guests. We hoped that these efforts in Canada would lead to a successful holiday season, but we did not see the required step-change in our holiday performance," said Cornell. "There is no doubt that the next several weeks will be difficult, but we will make every effort to handle our exit in an appropriate and orderly way.&#8221; </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">As a result of the CCAA filing, Target Corporation has determined that Target Canada and its subsidiaries will be deconsolidated from Target Corporation&#8217;s financial statements as of the date of the filing.  Target Corporation expects to report approximately $5.4 billion of pre-tax losses on discontinued operations in the fourth quarter of 2014, driven primarily by the write-down of the Corporation&#8217;s investment in Target Canada, along with costs associated with exit or </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:center;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8211; more &#8211;</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="sADE64D2CA3AB34478F71BFF72DF2D4EA"></a><div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div></div><br><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-style:italic;">Target Corporation Announces Plans to Discontinue Canadian Operations &#8211; Page 3 of 5</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">disposal activities and quarter-to-date Canadian Segment operating losses prior to today&#8217;s filing. Target Corporation expects to report approximately $275 million of pre-tax losses on discontinued operations in fiscal 2015.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Target Corporation&#8217;s cash costs to discontinue Canadian operations are expected to be $500 million to $600 million, most of which will occur in the Company&#8217;s 2015 fiscal year or later. The Company has sufficient resources to fund these expected costs, including cash on hand and ongoing cash generation by its U.S. business.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Target Corporation expects this decision will increase its earnings in fiscal 2015 and beyond, and increase its cash flow in fiscal 2016 and beyond.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">As a result of the decision announced today, Target Corporation will operate as a single segment that includes all U.S. operations. Beginning with the Company&#8217;s fourth quarter 2014 financial results, Target will report adjusted earnings per share reflecting operating results from its U.S. operations, excluding discontinued Canadian operations, the impact of the reduction of the beneficial interest asset recognized in connection with the 2013 sale of the Company&#8217;s U.S. consumer credit card portfolio, net expenses related to the 2013 data breach, and the resolution of certain tax matters.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Target Corporation plans to provide additional information on the financial implications of this announcement in a Form 8-K to be filed with the Securities and Exchange Commission later today.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-weight:bold;">Update on expected fourth quarter U.S. performance</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Based on performance through November and December, Target Corporation now expects to report fourth quarter 2014 U.S. comparable sales of approximately 3 percent, better than prior guidance of approximately 2 percent, driven primarily by increased traffic and </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:center;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8211; more &#8211;</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div &#8211; Page 4 of 5</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div The Company expects to report fourth quarter adjusted EPS, reflecting results from continuing operations, of $1.43 to $1.47, about 6 cents ahead of expectations for U.S. Segment performance at the beginning of the quarter.  </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">The Company is not able to provide an estimate of its expected fourth quarter 2014 GAAP EPS. However, GAAP results are expected to include:</font></div><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:50px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;padding-left:26px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Losses related to liquidation of Target Canada, as described above, net of taxes</font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; Prior to deconsolidation, these loans were considered intercompany notes payable by Target Canada and were eliminated in consolidation. Subsequent to the deconsolidation, these amounts are recorded as balances with Target Canada (related party notes receivable) at an estimated fair value based on the retained interest determined by the recoverability of the carrying amount and whether the related party notes receivable are considered secured or unsecured.  We have estimated a recovery rate based upon the estimated fair value of the net assets of Target Canada available for distribution in relation to the secured and unsecured claims in the CCAA filing. </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-style:italic;"><sup style="vertical-align:top;line-height:120%;font-size:7pt">(d)</sup></font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;&#32;Includes a liability for Target's expected cash contribution into a trust for the benefit of the employees of Target Canada.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-style:italic;"><sup style="vertical-align:top;line-height:120%;font-size:7pt">(e)</sup></font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;&#32;Includes contingent liabilities retained by Target Corporation after the deconsolidation.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-style:italic;"><sup style="vertical-align:top;line-height:120%;font-size:7pt">(f) </sup></font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#32;The adjustment to retained earnings includes the impairment loss on our investment in Target Canada and the estimated tax impact as a result of the deconsolidation. The unaudited pro forma consolidated statements of operations do not include the estimated impairment loss on our investment or the estimated tax impact because of their non-recurring nature.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><br><div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font
